This was true despite the fact that all the larger land masses involved (as well as many of the smaller ones) contained multiple climatic zones that would have been affected differently by any climate changes ongoing at the time. However, on sizable islands far enough offshore from newly occupied territory to escape immediate human colonization, megafaunal species sometimes survived for many thousands of years after they or related species became extinct on the mainland; examples include <a href="/wiki/Protemnodon" title="Protemnodon">giant kangaroos</a> in Tasmania,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamond_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond-135">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turney_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turney-136">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Giant_tortoise" title="Giant tortoise">giant</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Chelonoidis" title="Chelonoidis">Chelonoidis</a></i> tortoises of the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a> (formerly also of South America<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cione_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cione-88">[74]</a></sup>), giant <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dipsochelys" title="Dipsochelys">Dipsochelys</a></i> tortoises of the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> (formerly also of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>), giant <a href="/wiki/Meiolania" title="Meiolania">meiolaniid turtles</a> on <a href="/wiki/Lord_Howe_Island" title="Lord Howe Island">Lord Howe Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_New_Caledonia" title="Biodiversity of New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> (previously also of Australia),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-White-137">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[n 25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Megalocnus" title="Megalocnus">ground sloths</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_sea_cow" title="Steller's sea cow">Steller's sea cows</a> off the <a href="/wiki/Commander_Islands" title="Commander Islands">Commander Islands</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Woolly_mammoth" title="Woolly mammoth">woolly mammoths</a> on <a href="/wiki/Wrangel_Island" title="Wrangel Island">Wrangel Island</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vartanyan1_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vartanyan1-143">[118]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul_Island_(Alaska)" title="Saint Paul Island (Alaska)">Saint Paul Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[119]</a></sup> The glacial retreat may have played a primarily indirect role in the extinctions in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> by simply facilitating the movement of humans southeastward from <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Beringia</a> down to North America. The reason that a number of groups went extinct in North America but lived on in South America (while there are no examples of the opposite pattern) appears to be that the dense rainforest of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon basin</a> and the high peaks of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> provided environments that afforded a degree of protection from human predation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islands.26continents_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-islands.26continents-145">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[n 26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[n 27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_American_invasions_of_North_America_exclusive_of_Central_America">South American invasions of North America exclusive of Central America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_American_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: South American invasions of North America exclusive of Central America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extant_taxon" title="Extant taxon">Extant</a> or <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinct</a> (†) North American <a href="/wiki/Taxon" title="Taxon">taxa</a> whose ancestors migrated out of South America:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qualifier_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-qualifier-148">[n 28]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cichlids" title="Cichlids">Cichlids</a> (Cichlidae: e.g. <a href="/wiki/Texas_cichlid" title="Texas cichlid">Texas cichlid</a>) – <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_fish" title="Freshwater fish">freshwater fish</a> that often tolerate <a href="/wiki/Brackish_water" title="Brackish water">brackish</a> conditions</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bufonidae" title="Bufonidae">Bufonid toads</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bufo" title="Bufo">Bufo</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webb_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Webb-149">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pauly_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pauly-150">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hylidae" title="Hylidae">Hylid frogs</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leptodactylidae" title="Leptodactylidae">Leptodactylid frogs</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinicke_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heinicke-152">[124]</a></sup> – as far north as <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microhylidae" title="Microhylidae">Microhylid frogs</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webb_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-Webb-149">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virginia_opossum" title="Virginia opossum">Virginia opossum</a> (<i>Didelphis virginiana</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">Armadillos</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nine-banded_armadillo" title="Nine-banded armadillo">nine-banded armadillo</a> <i>Dasypus novemcinctus</i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Dasypus_bellus" title="Dasypus bellus">D. bellus</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<i><a href="/wiki/Pachyarmatherium" title="Pachyarmatherium">Pachyarmatherium</a> leiseyi</i>, an enigmatic armored armadillo relative</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Pampatheriidae" title="Pampatheriidae">Pampatheres</a> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plaina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plaina (page does not exist)">Plaina</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Casteneda_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Casteneda-153">[125]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Holmesina" title="Holmesina">Holmesina</a></i>) – large armadillo-like animals</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Glyptodont" title="Glyptodont">Glyptodonts</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Glyptotherium" title="Glyptotherium">Glyptotherium</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalonychid_ground_sloth" title="Megalonychid ground sloth">Megalonychid ground sloths</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[n 29]</a></sup> (<i><a href="/wiki/Pliometanastes" title="Pliometanastes">Pliometanastes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Megalonyx" title="Megalonyx">Megalonyx</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Ground_sloth#Mylodontidae" title="Ground sloth">Mylodontid ground sloths</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Thinobadistes" title="Thinobadistes">Thinobadistes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Glossotherium" title="Glossotherium">Glossotherium</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Casteneda_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-Casteneda-153">[125]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Paramylodon" title="Paramylodon">Paramylodon</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Ground_sloth#Megatheriidae" title="Ground sloth">Megatheriid ground sloths</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Eremotherium" title="Eremotherium">Eremotherium</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Ground_sloth#Nothrotheriidae" title="Ground sloth">Nothrotheriid ground sloths</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Nothrotheriops" title="Nothrotheriops">Nothrotheriops</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Nothrotherium" title="Nothrotherium">Nothrotherium</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_World_porcupine" title="New World porcupine">New World porcupines</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/North_American_porcupine" title="North American porcupine">Erethizon dorsatum</a></i>, †<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Erethizon_poyeri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Erethizon poyeri (page does not exist)">Erethizon poyeri</a></i>, †<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Erethizon_kleini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Erethizon kleini (page does not exist)">E. kleini</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capybara" title="Capybara">Capybaras</a> (†<i><a href="/wiki/Neochoerus_pinckneyi" title="Neochoerus pinckneyi">Neochoerus pinckneyi</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Neochoerus_aesopi" title="Neochoerus aesopi">N. aesopi</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<i><a href="/wiki/Mixotoxodon" title="Mixotoxodon">Mixotoxodon</a></i> – a rhino-sized <a href="/wiki/Toxodontidae" title="Toxodontidae">toxodontid</a> <a href="/wiki/Notoungulata" title="Notoungulata">notoungulate</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[n 30]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">Cougar</a> (<i>Puma concolor</i>) – returning from a South American <a href="/wiki/Refugium_(population_biology)" title="Refugium (population biology)">refugium</a> after North American cougars were <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">extirpated</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_extinction_event" title="Quaternary extinction event">Pleistocene extinctions</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[128]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molossidae" title="Molossidae">Molossid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lim2009_49-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lim2009-49">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mormoopidae" title="Mormoopidae">Mormoopid</a> bats (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormoops_megalophylla" title="Mormoops megalophylla">Mormoops megalophylla</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunnell2014_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gunnell2014-50">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vampire_bat" title="Vampire bat">Vampire bats</a> (†<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desmodus_stocki" title="Desmodus stocki">Desmodus stocki</a></i>, †<i>D. archaeodaptes</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Parrot" title="Parrot">Parrots</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotropical_parrots" title="Neotropical parrots">Neotropical parrots</a>: <a href="/wiki/Thick-billed_parrot" title="Thick-billed parrot">thick-billed parrot</a>, †<a href="/wiki/Carolina_parakeet" title="Carolina parakeet">Carolina parakeet</a>)</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Phorusrhacidae" title="Phorusrhacidae">Terror birds</a> (Phorusrhacidae: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Titanis_walleri" title="Titanis walleri">Titanis walleri</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tanager" title="Tanager">Tanagers</a> (Thraupidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ricklefs2002_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ricklefs2002-160">[130]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hummingbird" title="Hummingbird">Hummingbirds</a> (Trochilidae)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suboscine_bird" title="Suboscine bird">Suboscine birds</a> (Tyranni):
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tityras_and_allies" title="Tityras and allies">Tityras and allies</a> (Tityridae): <a href="/wiki/Rose-throated_becard" title="Rose-throated becard">rose-throated becard</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tyrant_flycatcher" title="Tyrant flycatcher">Tyrant flycatchers</a> (Tyrannidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_American_invasions_that_only_extended_to_Central_America">South American invasions that only extended to Central America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_American_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: South American invasions that only extended to Central America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Extant or extinct (†) Central American taxa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[n 31]</a></sup> whose ancestors migrated out of South America:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qualifier_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-qualifier-148">[n 28]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Gonyleptid <a href="/wiki/Opiliones" title="Opiliones">harvestmen</a> (Opiliones: <a href="/wiki/Gonyleptidae" title="Gonyleptidae">Gonyleptidae</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gymnotiformes" title="Gymnotiformes">Electric knifefishes</a> (Gymnotiformes)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hoplosternum_punctatum" title="Hoplosternum punctatum">Hoplosternum punctatum</a></i>, an armored catfish (Siluriformes: <a href="/wiki/Callichthyidae" title="Callichthyidae">Callichthyidae</a>)</li>
<li>Several species of loricariid catfish (Siluriformes: <a href="/wiki/Loricariidae" title="Loricariidae">Loricariidae</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caeciliidae" title="Caeciliidae">Caeciliid</a> <a href="/wiki/Caecilian" title="Caecilian">caecilians</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Caecilia" title="Caecilia">Caecilia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Oscaecilia" title="Oscaecilia">Oscaecilia</a></i>) – snake-like amphibians, Panama and Costa Rica only<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-early_amphibians_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-early_amphibians-162">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Poison_dart_frog" title="Poison dart frog">Poison dart frogs</a> (Dendrobatidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>Boine <a href="/wiki/Boidae" title="Boidae">boas</a> (Boidae: <a href="/wiki/Boinae" title="Boinae">Boinae</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spectacled_caiman" title="Spectacled caiman">Spectacled caiman</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caimaninae" title="Caimaninae">Caiman</a> crocodilus</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossums</a> (Didelphidae) – 11 additional extant species<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAlisting_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-CAlisting-101">[n 19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_naked-tailed_armadillo" title="Northern naked-tailed armadillo">Northern naked-tailed armadillo</a> (<i>Cabassous centralis</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hoffmann%27s_two-toed_sloth" title="Hoffmann's two-toed sloth">Hoffmann's</a> <a href="/wiki/Two-toed_sloth" title="Two-toed sloth">two-toed sloth</a> (Megalonychidae: <i>Choloepus hoffmanni</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Three-toed_sloth" title="Three-toed sloth">Three-toed sloths</a> (Bradypodidae: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown-throated_three-toed_sloth" title="Brown-throated three-toed sloth"><i>Bradypus variegatus</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_three-toed_sloth" title="Pygmy three-toed sloth"><i>B. pygmaeus</i></a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silky_anteater" title="Silky anteater">Silky anteater</a> (Cyclopedidae: <i>Cyclopes didactylus</i>)</li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Myrmecophagidae" title="Myrmecophagidae">anteaters</a> (Myrmecophagidae: <a href="/wiki/Giant_anteater" title="Giant anteater"><i>Myrmecophaga tridactyla</i></a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[n 32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tamandua" title="Tamandua"><i>Tamandua mexicana</i></a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rothschild%27s_porcupine" title="Rothschild's porcupine">Rothschild's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexican_hairy_dwarf_porcupine" title="Mexican hairy dwarf porcupine">Mexican hairy dwarf</a> <a href="/wiki/New_World_porcupine" title="New World porcupine">porcupines</a> (<i>Coendou rothschildi</i>, <i>Sphiggurus mexicanus</i>)</li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Caviomorpha" title="Caviomorpha">caviomorph rodents</a> (Caviomorpha) – 9 additional extant species<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAlisting_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-CAlisting-101">[n 19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_World_monkey" title="New World monkey">Platyrrhine monkeys</a> (Platyrrhini) – at least 8 extant species<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAlisting_101-3"><a href="#cite_note-CAlisting-101">[n 19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[n 33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emballonuridae" title="Emballonuridae">Emballonurid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Teeling2005_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Teeling2005-51">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Furipteridae" title="Furipteridae">Furipterid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunnell2014_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gunnell2014-50">[44]</a></sup> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Furipterus_horrens" title="Furipterus horrens">Furipterus horrens</a></i>)</li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Mormoopidae" title="Mormoopidae">mormoopid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunnell2014_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-Gunnell2014-50">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noctilionidae" title="Noctilionidae">Noctilionid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunnell2014_50-4"><a href="#cite_note-Gunnell2014-50">[44]</a></sup> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noctilio_albiventris" title="Noctilio albiventris">Noctilio albiventris</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noctilio_leporinus" title="Noctilio leporinus">Noctilio leporinus</a></i>)</li>
<li>Other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phyllostomidae" title="Phyllostomidae">phyllostomid</a> bats,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunnell2014_50-5"><a href="#cite_note-Gunnell2014-50">[44]</a></sup> including all 3 extant <a href="/wiki/Vampire_bat" title="Vampire bat">vampire bat</a> species (Desmodontinae)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thyropteridae" title="Thyropteridae">Thyropterid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gunnell2014_50-6"><a href="#cite_note-Gunnell2014-50">[44]</a></sup> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thyroptera_discifera" title="Thyroptera discifera">Thyroptera discifera</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thyroptera_tricolor" title="Thyroptera tricolor">Thyroptera tricolor</a></i>)</li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Neotropical_parrot" title="Neotropical parrot">Neotropical parrots</a> (Arinae)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_curassow" title="Great curassow">Great curassow</a> (<i>Crax rubra</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toucan" title="Toucan">Toucans</a> (Ramphastidae)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tinamou" title="Tinamou">Tinamous</a> (Tinamidae)</li>
<li>Additional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suboscine_bird" title="Suboscine bird">suboscine birds</a> (Tyranni):
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gnateater" title="Gnateater">Gnateaters</a> (Conopophagidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cotinga" title="Cotinga">Cotingas</a> (Cotingidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-3"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_antbird" title="Ground antbird">Ground antbirds</a> (Formicariidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-4"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ovenbird_(family)" title="Ovenbird (family)">Ovenbirds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodcreeper" title="Woodcreeper">woodcreepers</a> (Furnariidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irestedt2002_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Irestedt2002-169">[136]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antpitta" title="Antpitta">Antpittas</a> (Grallariidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-5"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manakin" title="Manakin">Manakins</a> (Pipridae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-6"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tapaculo" title="Tapaculo">Tapaculos</a> (Rhinocryptidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-7"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antbird" title="Antbird">Antbirds</a> (Thamnophilidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-8"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_American_invasions_of_South_America">North American invasions of South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_American_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: North American invasions of South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Extant or extinct (†) South American taxa whose ancestors migrated out of North America (considered as including Central America):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qualifier_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-qualifier-148">[n 28]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dermophiidae" title="Dermophiidae">Dermophiid</a> <a href="/wiki/Caecilian" title="Caecilian">caecilians</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Dermophis_glandulosus" title="Dermophis glandulosus">Dermophis glandulosus</a></i>) – only present in northwestern Colombia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savage2001_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Savage2001-170">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lungless_salamander" title="Lungless salamander">Lungless salamanders</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[n 34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-early_amphibians_162-2"><a href="#cite_note-early_amphibians-162">[131]</a></sup> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bolitoglossa" title="Bolitoglossa">Bolitoglossa</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elmer2013_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elmer2013-171">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[139]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Oedipina" title="Oedipina">Oedipina</a></i>) – only present in northern South America</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ranidae" title="Ranidae">Ranid frogs</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webb_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-Webb-149">[121]</a></sup> – only present in northern South America</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chelydridae" title="Chelydridae">Chelydrid</a> (snapping) turtles (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chelydra_acutirostris" title="Chelydra acutirostris">Chelydra acutirostris</a></i>) – only present in northwestern South America</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emydidae" title="Emydidae">Emydid</a> (pond) turtles (<i><a href="/wiki/Trachemys" title="Trachemys">Trachemys</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Geoemydidae" title="Geoemydidae">Geoemydid</a> (wood) turtles (<i><a href="/wiki/Rhinoclemmys" title="Rhinoclemmys">Rhinoclemmys</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[140]</a></sup> – only present in northern South America</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coral_snake" title="Coral snake">Coral snakes</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leptomicrurus" title="Leptomicrurus">Leptomicrurus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Micrurus" title="Micrurus">Micrurus</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[142]</a></sup></li>
<li>South American <a href="/wiki/Rattlesnake" title="Rattlesnake">rattlesnake</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Crotalus_durissus" title="Crotalus durissus">Crotalus durissus</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li>Lanceheads (<i><a href="/wiki/Bothrops" title="Bothrops">Bothrops</a></i>)</li>
<li>Bushmasters (<i><a href="/wiki/Lachesis_(genus)" title="Lachesis (genus)">Lachesis</a></i>)</li>
<li>Other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crotalinae" title="Crotalinae">pit vipers</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bothriechis_schlegelii" title="Bothriechis schlegelii">Bothriechis schlegelii</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bothriopsis" title="Bothriopsis">Bothriopsis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Porthidium" title="Porthidium">Porthidium</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Small-eared_shrew" title="Small-eared shrew">Small-eared shrews</a> (<i>Cryptotis</i>) – only present in NW South America: Colombia, Venezuela, Ecuador, Peru</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pocket_gopher" title="Pocket gopher">Geomyid pocket gophers</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Thaeler%27s_pocket_gopher" title="Thaeler's pocket gopher">Orthogeomys thaeleri</a></i>) – one species, in Colombia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heteromyidae" title="Heteromyidae">Heteromyid mice</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Heteromys" title="Heteromys">Heteromys</a></i>) – only present in NW South America: Colombia, Venezuela, Ecuador</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_World_rats_and_mice" title="New World rats and mice">Cricetid</a> – primarily <a href="/wiki/Sigmodontinae" title="Sigmodontinae">sigmodontine</a> – rats and mice (Cricetidae: Sigmodontinae) – the nonsigmodontines consist of two species present only in Colombia and Ecuador<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[n 35]</a></sup></li>
<li>Tree <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sciuridae" title="Sciuridae">squirrels</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sciurus" title="Sciurus">Sciurus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Microsciurus" title="Microsciurus">Microsciurus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Neotropical_pygmy_squirrel" title="Neotropical pygmy squirrel">Sciurillus</a></i>) – present in northern and central South America</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cottontail_rabbit" title="Cottontail rabbit">Cottontail</a> <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbits</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tapeti" title="Tapeti"><i>Sylvilagus brasiliensis</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_cottontail" title="Eastern cottontail"><i>S. floridanus</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_lowland_rabbit" title="Venezuelan lowland rabbit"><i>S. varynaensis</i></a>) – present in northern and central South America</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tapir" title="Tapir">Tapirs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Baird%27s_tapir" title="Baird's tapir"><i>Tapirus bairdii</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tapirus_kabomani" title="Tapirus kabomani">T. kabomani</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_tapir" title="Mountain tapir"><i>T. pinchaque</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_tapir" title="Brazilian tapir"><i>T. terrestris</i></a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Equidae" title="Equidae">Equids</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equus_ferus" title="Equus ferus">Equus ferus</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Hippidion" title="Hippidion">Hippidion</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[n 36]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peccary" title="Peccary">Peccaries</a> (†<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sylvochoerus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sylvochoerus (page does not exist)">Sylvochoerus</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frailey2012_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Frailey2012-72">[63]</a></sup> †<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Waldochoerus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Waldochoerus (page does not exist)">Waldochoerus</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frailey2012_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-Frailey2012-72">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/White-lipped_peccary" title="White-lipped peccary"><i>Tayassu pecari</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Chacoan_peccary" title="Chacoan peccary"><i>Catagonus wagneri</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Collared_peccary" title="Collared peccary"><i>Pecari tajacu</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Giant_peccary" title="Giant peccary"><i>P. maximus</i></a>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeomerycid" title="Palaeomerycid">Palaeomerycids</a> (†<i><a href="/wiki/Surameryx" title="Surameryx">Surameryx</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prothero2014_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prothero2014-73">[64]</a></sup>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">Deer</a> (†<i><a href="/wiki/Antifer" title="Antifer">Antifer</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer"><i>Odocoileus</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Marsh_deer" title="Marsh deer"><i>Blastocerus</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Pampas_deer" title="Pampas deer"><i>Ozotoceros</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Brocket_deer" title="Brocket deer"><i>Mazama</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Pud%C3%BA" title="Pudú"><i>Pudu</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hippocamelus" title="Hippocamelus">Hippocamelus</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Camelid" title="Camelid">Camelids</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guanaco" title="Guanaco"><i>Lama guanicoe</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicu%C3%B1a" title="Vicuña"><i>Vicugna vicugna</i></a>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Eulamaops" title="Eulamaops">Eulamaops</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Hemiauchenia" title="Hemiauchenia">Hemiauchenia</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Palaeolama" title="Palaeolama">Palaeolama</a></i>)</li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Gomphothere" title="Gomphothere">Gomphotheres</a> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amahuacatherium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amahuacatherium (page does not exist)">Amahuacatherium</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell2000_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2000-68">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell2009_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2009-69">[61]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Cuvieronius" title="Cuvieronius">Cuvieronius</a> hyodon</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Stegomastodon" title="Stegomastodon">Stegomastodon</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[n 37]</a></sup> <i>waringi</i>, <i>S. platensis</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prado_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prado-121">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[n 38]</a></sup> – <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephant</a> relatives</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otter" title="Otter">Otters</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Lontra" title="Lontra">Lontra</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Giant_otter" title="Giant otter">Pteronura</a></i>)</li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Mustelidae" title="Mustelidae">mustelids</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mustelinae" title="Mustelinae">Mustelinae</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Tayra" title="Tayra">Eira</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Galictis" title="Galictis">Galictis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Patagonian_weasel" title="Patagonian weasel">Lyncodon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Weasel" title="Weasel">Mustela</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hog-nosed_skunk" title="Hog-nosed skunk">Hog-nosed</a> <a href="/wiki/Skunk" title="Skunk">skunks</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Molina%27s_hog-nosed_skunk" title="Molina's hog-nosed skunk">Conepatus chinga</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Humboldt%27s_hog-nosed_skunk" title="Humboldt's hog-nosed skunk">C. humboldtii</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Striped_hog-nosed_skunk" title="Striped hog-nosed skunk">C. semistriatus</a></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Procyonidae" title="Procyonidae">Procyonids</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Procyon_(genus)" title="Procyon (genus)">Procyon</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Coati" title="Coati"><i>Nasua</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountain_coati" title="Mountain coati"><i>Nasuella</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Kinkajou" title="Kinkajou"><i>Potos</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olingo" title="Olingo"><i>Bassaricyon</i></a>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Cyonasua" title="Cyonasua">Cyonasua</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Chapalmalania" title="Chapalmalania">Chapalmalania</a></i>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctodus" title="Arctodus">Short-faced bears</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tremarctinae" title="Tremarctinae">Tremarctinae</a>: <a href="/wiki/Spectacled_bear" title="Spectacled bear"><i>Tremarctos ornatus</i></a>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Arctotherium" title="Arctotherium">Arctotherium</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[148]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canis#Coyotes.2C_jackals.2C_and_wolves" title="Canis">Wolves</a> (†<i>Canis gezi</i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Canis_nehringi" title="Canis nehringi">C. nehringi</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Dire_wolf" title="Dire wolf">C. dirus</a></i> – the latter known only from as far south as southern Bolivia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paleobiology_Cdirus_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-paleobiology_Cdirus-187">[149]</a></sup>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HodnettMead2009_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-HodnettMead2009-188">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Berta1988_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Berta1988-189">[151]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gray_fox" title="Gray fox">Gray fox</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[n 39]</a></sup> (<i>Urocyon cinereoargenteus</i>) – only present in NW South America: Colombia, Venezuela</li>
<li>Other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canids" title="Canids">canids</a> (†<i><a href="/wiki/Dusicyon" title="Dusicyon">Dusicyon</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Httpwwwsciencedailycomreleaseshtm_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Httpwwwsciencedailycomreleaseshtm-191">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cooper_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-cooper-192">[153]</a></sup> †<i><a href="/wiki/Theriodictis" title="Theriodictis">Theriodictis</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Protocyon" title="Protocyon">Protocyon</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Short-eared_dog" title="Short-eared dog"><i>Atelocynus</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Crab-eating_fox" title="Crab-eating fox"><i>Cerdocyon</i></a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lycalopex" title="Lycalopex">Lycalopex</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Maned_wolf" title="Maned wolf"><i>Chrysocyon</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Bush_dog" title="Bush dog"><i>Speothos</i></a>)</li>
<li>Small <a href="/wiki/Felidae" title="Felidae">felids</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Leopardus" title="Leopardus">Leopardus</a></i>) – all 9 extant species (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Ocelot" title="Ocelot"><i>L. pardalis</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Margay" title="Margay"><i>L. wiedii</i></a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">Cougar</a> (<i>Puma concolor</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Jaguarundi" title="Jaguarundi">jaguarundi</a> (<i>P. yagouaroundi)</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">Jaguar</a> (<i>Panthera onca</i>)</li>
<li>†Scimitar cats (<i><a href="/wiki/Xenosmilus" title="Xenosmilus">Xenosmilus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Homotherium" title="Homotherium">Homotherium</a></i>) – known so far only from Uruguay<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mones2004_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mones2004-193">[154]</a></sup> and Venezuela<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rinc.C3.B3nPrevosti2011_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rinc.C3.B3nPrevosti2011-196">[157]</a></sup></li>
<li>†<a href="/wiki/Smilodon" title="Smilodon">Saber-toothed cats</a> (<i>Smilodon gracilis</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rinc.C3.B3nPrevosti2011_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rinc.C3.B3nPrevosti2011-196">[157]</a></sup> <i>S. fatalis</i>, <i>S. populator</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Natalidae" title="Natalidae">Natalid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lim2009_49-6"><a href="#cite_note-Lim2009-49">[43]</a></sup> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chilonatalus_micropus" title="Chilonatalus micropus">Chilonatalus micropus</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natalus_espiritosantensis" title="Natalus espiritosantensis">Natalus espiritosantensis</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natalus_tumidirostris" title="Natalus tumidirostris">N. tumidirostris</a></i>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vespertilionidae" title="Vespertilionidae">Vespertilionid</a> bats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lim2009_49-7"><a href="#cite_note-Lim2009-49">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_sparrow" title="American sparrow">American sparrows</a> (Emberizidae)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeirBermingham2009_159-9"><a href="#cite_note-WeirBermingham2009-159">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EricsonChristidis2002_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-EricsonChristidis2002-197">[158]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trogon" title="Trogon">Trogons</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Trogon_(genus)" title="Trogon (genus)">Trogon</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[159]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Condor" title="Condor">Condors</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Andean_condor" title="Andean condor">Vultur gryphus</a></i>, †<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dryornis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dryornis (page does not exist)">Dryornis</a></i>, †<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Geronogyps&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Geronogyps (page does not exist)">Geronogyps</a></i>, †<i><a href="/wiki/Wingegyps" title="Wingegyps">Wingegyps</a></i>, †<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Perugyps&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Perugyps (page does not exist)">Perugyps</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hadrogyps_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hadrogyps-200">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Condor_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Condor-201">[162]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[n 40]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_American_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a>, astrapotheres<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bond2011_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bond2011-8">[8]</a></sup> and litopterns<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bond2006_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bond2006-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gelfo2015_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gelfo2015-10">[10]</a></sup> were also present in Antarctica.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sequencing of <a href="/wiki/Collagen" title="Collagen">collagen</a> from fossils of one recently extinct species each of notoungulates and litopterns has indicated that these orders comprise a <a href="/wiki/Sister_group" title="Sister group">sister group</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perissodactyl" title="Perissodactyl">perissodactyls</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WelkerCollins2015_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-WelkerCollins2015-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buckley2015_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley2015-13">[12]</a></sup> Mitochondrial DNA obtained from <i><a href="/wiki/Macrauchenia" title="Macrauchenia">Macrauchenia</a></i> corroborates this and gives an estimated divergence date of 66 Ma ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Westbury2017_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Westbury2017-14">[13]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Once in Australia, facing less competition, marsupials diversified to fill a much larger array of niches than in South America, where they were largely carnivorous.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is the <a href="/wiki/Sister_group" title="Sister group">sister group</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Clade" title="Clade">clade</a> containing all other extant australidelphians (roughly 238 species).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ziphodont (lateromedially compressed, recurved and serrated) teeth tend to arise in terrestrial crocodilians because, unlike their aquatic cousins, they are unable to dispatch their prey by simply holding them underwater and drowning them; they thus need cutting teeth with which to slice open their victims.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is also notable that both <a href="/wiki/Simian" title="Simian">simian primates</a> (ancestral to monkeys) and <a href="/wiki/Hystricognathi" title="Hystricognathi">hystricognath</a> rodents (ancestral to caviomorphs) are believed to have arrived in Africa by rafting from Eurasia about 40 Ma ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaimanee_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chaimanee-47">[42]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">North American <a href="/wiki/Gopherus" title="Gopherus">gopher tortoises</a> are most closely related to the Asian genus <i><a href="/wiki/Manouria" title="Manouria">Manouria</a></i>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An alternative explanation blames climatic and physiographic changes associated with the uplift of the Andes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gasparini_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gasparini-29">[24]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-71">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The status of <i>Amahuacatherium</i> is controversial, and it is sometimes considered as a misinterpreted fossil of a Pleistocene gomphothere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prado2005_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prado2005-70">[62]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Of the 6 families of North American rodents that did not originate in South America, only <a href="/wiki/Beaver" title="Beaver">beavers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mountain_beaver" title="Mountain beaver">mountain beavers</a> failed to migrate to South America. (However, human-introduced beavers have become serious <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>.)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Simpson, 1950, p. 382<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_History_1950_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson_History_1950-79">[69]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Marshall, 1988, p. 386<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LandMammals_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-LandMammals-3">[3]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Of the 11 extant families of South American caviomorph rodents, 5 are present in Central America; only 2 of these, <a href="/wiki/New_World_porcupine" title="New World porcupine">Erethizontidae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caviidae" title="Caviidae">Caviidae</a>, ever reached North America. (The <a href="/wiki/Coypu" title="Coypu">nutria/coypu</a> has been introduced to a number of North American locales.)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The dog-like <a href="/wiki/Borhyaenidae" title="Borhyaenidae">borhyaenids</a> were already in decline before the main pulse of the interchange, at a time when <i>Thylacosmilus</i> and phorusrhacids were still common. Suggested reasons for this decline include competition with phorusrhacids, carnivorous opossums, or early-arriving procyonids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Argot_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Argot-83">[70]</a></sup> However, it is clear that the remaining sparassodonts and most of the phorusrhacids (<i>Titanis</i> being an exception) disappeared quickly once canids and felids reached South America.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">P. S. Martin (2005), pp. 30–37, 119.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-89">[75]</a></sup> The figure of 25 South American megaherbivore species breaks down as follows: 4 gomphotheres, 2 camelids, 9 ground sloths, 5 glyptodonts, and 5 toxodontids. This can be compared to Africa's present and recent total of 6 megaherbivores: 1 giraffe, 1 hippo, 2 rhinos and 2 elephants (considering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loxodonta_cyclotis" title="Loxodonta cyclotis">African forest elephant</a> as a separate species).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-canidlisting-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-canidlisting_93-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-canidlisting_93-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extant_taxon" title="Extant taxon">extant</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canid" title="Canid">canid</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cervid" title="Cervid">cervid</a> genera by continent are as follows:</span>
<div style="color: #000000; background: none; overflow: hidden; page-break-after: avoid; font-size: 100%; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 0.3em; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: 1.6; padding-top: 0.5em; padding-bottom: 0;"><span class="reference-text">Canid genera by continent</span></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">North America: 3 genera, 9 species – <i><a href="/wiki/Canis" title="Canis">Canis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Urocyon" title="Urocyon">Urocyon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vulpes" title="Vulpes">Vulpes</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Central America: 3 genera, 4 species – <i><a href="/wiki/Canis" title="Canis">Canis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Speothos" title="Speothos">Speothos</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Urocyon" title="Urocyon">Urocyon</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">South America: 6 genera, 11 species – <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atelocynus" title="Atelocynus">Atelocynus</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerdocyon" title="Cerdocyon">Cerdocyon</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chrysocyon" title="Chrysocyon">Chrysocyon</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lycalopex" title="Lycalopex">Lycalopex</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Speothos" title="Speothos">Speothos</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Urocyon" title="Urocyon">Urocyon</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Eurasia: 4 genera, 12 species – <i><a href="/wiki/Canis" title="Canis">Canis</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuon" title="Cuon">Cuon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Nyctereutes" title="Nyctereutes">Nyctereutes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vulpes" title="Vulpes">Vulpes</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Africa: 4 genera, 12 species – <i><a href="/wiki/Canis" title="Canis">Canis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lycaon_(genus)" title="Lycaon (genus)">Lycaon</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otocyon" title="Otocyon">Otocyon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vulpes" title="Vulpes">Vulpes</a></i></span></li>
</ul>
<div style="color: #000000; background: none; overflow: hidden; page-break-after: avoid; font-size: 100%; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 0.3em; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: 1.6; padding-top: 0.5em; padding-bottom: 0;"><span class="reference-text">Cervid genera by continent</span></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">North America: 4 genera, 5 species – <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alces" title="Alces">Alces</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cervus" title="Cervus">Cervus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Odocoileus" title="Odocoileus">Odocoileus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">Rangifer</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Central America: 2 genera, 4 species – <i><a href="/wiki/Brocket_deer" title="Brocket deer">Mazama</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Odocoileus" title="Odocoileus">Odocoileus</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">South America: 6 genera, 16 species – <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blastocerus" title="Blastocerus">Blastocerus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hippocamelus" title="Hippocamelus">Hippocamelus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Brocket_deer" title="Brocket deer">Mazama</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Odocoileus" title="Odocoileus">Odocoileus</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ozotoceros" title="Ozotoceros">Ozotoceros</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pud%C3%BA" title="Pudú">Pudu</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Eurasia: 10 genera, 36 species – <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alces" title="Alces">Alces</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_(genus)" title="Axis (genus)">Axis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Capreolus" title="Capreolus">Capreolus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cervus" title="Cervus">Cervus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fallow_deer" title="Fallow deer">Dama</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elaphodus" title="Elaphodus">Elaphodus</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elaphurus" title="Elaphurus">Elaphurus</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydropotes" title="Hydropotes">Hydropotes</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muntiacus" title="Muntiacus">Muntiacus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">Rangifer</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Africa: 1 genus, 1 species – <i><a href="/wiki/Cervus" title="Cervus">Cervus</a></i></span></li>
</ul>
<div style="color: #000000; background: none; overflow: hidden; page-break-after: avoid; font-size: 100%; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 0.3em; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: 1.6; padding-top: 0.5em; padding-bottom: 0;"></div>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Including extinct genera, South America has hosted 9 genera of cervids, 8 genera of mustelids, and 10 genera of canids. However, some of this diversity of South American forms apparently arose in North or Central America prior to the interchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GAIpatterns_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-GAIpatterns-77">[67]</a></sup> There is significant disagreement in the literature concerning how much of the diversification of South America's canids occurred prior to the invasions. A number of studies concur that the grouping of endemic South American canids (excluding <i>Urocyon</i> and <i>Canis</i>, although sometimes transferring <i>C. gezi</i> to the South American group<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prevosti2010_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prevosti2010-94">[78]</a></sup>) is a clade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prevosti2010_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prevosti2010-94">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PeriniRusso2010_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-PeriniRusso2010-95">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SlaterThalmann2009_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-SlaterThalmann2009-96">[80]</a></sup> However, different authors conclude that members of this clade reached South America in at least two,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PeriniRusso2010_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-PeriniRusso2010-95">[79]</a></sup> three to four,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prevosti2010_94-2"><a href="#cite_note-Prevosti2010-94">[78]</a></sup> or six<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SlaterThalmann2009_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-SlaterThalmann2009-96">[80]</a></sup> invasions from North America.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-98">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Canis</i>, e.g. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canis_dirus" title="Canis dirus">Canis dirus</a></i>, was present in South America until the end of the Pleistocene.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-CAlisting-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CAlisting_101-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CAlisting_101-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CAlisting_101-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CAlisting_101-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The Central American species of South American origin (<a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xenarthra" title="Xenarthra">xenarthrans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caviomorph_rodent" title="Caviomorph rodent">caviomorph rodents</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platyrrhine_monkey" title="Platyrrhine monkey">platyrrhine monkeys</a>) are as follows:</span>

<div style="color: #000000; background: none; overflow: hidden; page-break-after: avoid; font-size: 100%; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 0.3em; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: 1.6; padding-top: 0.5em; padding-bottom: 0;"></div>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> alone, between about 23 and 5 Ma ago, 11 episodes of invasions of North America from Eurasia have been recognized, bringing a total of 81 new genera into North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GAIpatterns_77-3"><a href="#cite_note-GAIpatterns-77">[67]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-103">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The combination of Africa, Eurasia and North America was termed the "World Continent" by <a href="/wiki/George_Gaylord_Simpson" title="George Gaylord Simpson">George Gaylord Simpson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_History_1950_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson_History_1950-79">[69]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-104">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Simpson, 1950, p. 368<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_History_1950_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson_History_1950-79">[69]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to data on the EQ (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_to_body_mass_ratio" title="Brain to body mass ratio">encephalization quotient</a>, a measure of the brain to body size ratio adjusted for the expected effect of differences in body size) of fossil ungulates compiled by H. Jerison,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAungulates_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAungulates-107">[85]</a></sup> North American ungulates showed a trend towards greater EQs going from the <a href="/wiki/Paleogene" title="Paleogene">Paleogene</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Neogene" title="Neogene">Neogene</a> periods (average EQs of 0.43 and 0.64, respectively), while the EQs of South American ungulates were static over the same time interval (average EQ unchanged at 0.48).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GGSimpson_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-GGSimpson-7">[7]</a></sup> This analysis was later criticized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radinsky1_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radinsky1-108">[86]</a></sup> Jerison subsequently presented data suggesting that native South American ungulates also lagged in the relative size of their <a href="/wiki/Neocortex" title="Neocortex">neocortex</a> (a measurement not subject to the vagaries of body mass estimation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerison2_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jerison2-109">[87]</a></sup> It is interesting to note that the late survivor <i>Toxodon</i> had one of the highest EQ values (0.88) among native Neotropic ungulates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radinsky1_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Radinsky1-108">[86]</a></sup><br/>
Jerison also found that Neogene xenarthrans had low EQs, similar to those he obtained for South American ungulates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAungulates_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAungulates-107">[85]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-115">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The estimated EQ of <i>Thylacosmilus atrox</i>, 0.41 (based on a brain mass of 43.2 g, a body mass of 26.4 kg,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wroe_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wroe-111">[88]</a></sup> and an EQ of 43.2/[0.12*26400^(2/3)]<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerison2_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jerison2-109">[87]</a></sup>), is high for a sparassodont,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quiroga_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quiroga-112">[89]</a></sup> but is lower than that of modern felids, with a mean value of 0.87.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radinsky2_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radinsky2-113">[90]</a></sup> Estimates of 0.38<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerison_1973_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jerison_1973-114">[91]</a></sup> and 0.59<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radinsky2_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Radinsky2-113">[90]</a></sup> have been given for the EQ of much larger <i>Smilodon fatalis</i> (based on body mass estimates of 330 and 175 kg, respectively).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colossochelys_atlas" title="Colossochelys atlas">giant tortoises of Asia</a> and Africa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THarrison_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-THarrison-138">[114]</a></sup> died out much earlier in the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> than those of South America, Madagascar and Australia, while those of North America<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hansen_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hansen-139">[115]</a></sup> died out around the same time.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">P. S. Martin (2005), p. 175.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-89">[75]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-147">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A number of recently extinct North American (and in some cases also South American) taxa such as tapirs, equids, camelids, <a href="/wiki/Saiga_antelope" title="Saiga antelope">saiga antelope</a>, proboscids, dholes and lions survived in the Old World, probably mostly for different reasons – tapirs being a likely exception, since their <a href="/wiki/Malayan_tapir" title="Malayan tapir">Old World representative</a> survived only in the rainforests of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. (Cheetahs in the broadest sense could be added to this list, although the <a href="/wiki/American_cheetah" title="American cheetah">New</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheetah" title="Cheetah">Old World</a> forms are in different genera.) Old World herbivores may in many cases have been able to learn to be vigilant about the presence of humans during a more gradual appearance (by development or migration) of advanced human hunters in their ranges. In the cases of predators, the Old World representatives in at least some locations would thus have suffered less from extinctions of their prey species. In contrast, the <a href="/wiki/Muskox" title="Muskox">musk ox</a> represents a rare example of a megafaunal taxon that recently became extinct in Asia but survived in remote areas of <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">arctic</a> North America (its more southerly-distributed relatives such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harlan%27s_muskox" title="Harlan's muskox">Harlan's musk ox</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shrub-ox" title="Shrub-ox">shrub ox</a> were less fortunate).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-qualifier-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-qualifier_148-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-qualifier_148-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-qualifier_148-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">This listing currently has fairly complete coverage of mammals, but only spotty coverage of other groups. Crossings by nonflying mammals and birds occurred during the last 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annum" title="Annum">Ma</a>. Crossings by fish, arthropods, rafting amphibians and reptiles, and flying bats and birds were made before 10 Ma ago in many cases. Taxa listed as invasive did not necessarily cross the isthmus themselves; they may have evolved in the adopted land mass from ancestral taxa that made the crossing.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-154"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-154">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">While all megalonychid ground sloths are extinct, extant <a href="/wiki/Two-toed_sloth" title="Two-toed sloth">two-toed tree sloths</a> are from the same family. <a href="/wiki/Three-toed_sloth" title="Three-toed sloth">Three-toed tree sloths</a>, in contrast, are not closely related to any of the groups of extinct ground sloths.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Mixotoxodon</i> remains have been collected in Central America and Mexico as far north as <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michoac%C3%A1n" title="Michoacán">Michoacán</a>, with a possible find in <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mexico_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mexico-155">[126]</a></sup> additionally, one fossil tooth has been identified in eastern <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lundelius2013_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lundelius2013-156">[127]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-161"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-161">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For the purposes of this article, all northwardly migrating Neotropic taxa that failed to reach the territory of the continental U.S. will be treated as having only reached Central America. While Central America is usually defined <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">physiographically</a> as ending at the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">Isthmus of Tehuantepec</a>, or less commonly, at the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Mexican_Volcanic_Belt" title="Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt">Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt</a>, most of the taxa that proceeded further but failed to reach the present Mexican border are or were confined to tropical or subtropical ecozones similar to those of Central America. Examples include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myrmecophaga_tridactyla" title="Myrmecophaga tridactyla">giant anteater</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tlacuatzin_canescens" title="Tlacuatzin canescens">grayish mouse opossum</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuniculus_paca" title="Cuniculus paca">lowland paca</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ateles_geoffroyi" title="Ateles geoffroyi">Geoffroy's spider monkey</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-166"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-166">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Fossils of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myrmecophaga_tridactyla" title="Myrmecophaga tridactyla">giant anteater</a> have been found as far north as northwestern <a href="/wiki/Sonora" title="Sonora">Sonora</a>, Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shaw_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shaw-165">[134]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-168">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It has been proposed that monkeys invaded Central America in at least three and probably four waves, as follows: (1) an initial invasion by <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_black_howler" title="Guatemalan black howler"><i>A. pigra</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_American_squirrel_monkey" title="Central American squirrel monkey"><i>S. oerstedii</i></a> ~ 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megaannum" title="Megaannum">Ma</a> ago; (2) an invasion by <a href="/wiki/Mantled_howler" title="Mantled howler"><i>A. palliata</i></a> (giving rise to <a href="/wiki/Coiba_Island_howler" title="Coiba Island howler"><i>A. coibensis</i></a>), <a href="/wiki/Geoffroy%27s_spider_monkey" title="Geoffroy's spider monkey"><i>A. geoffroyi</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/White-headed_capuchin" title="White-headed capuchin"><i>C. capucinus</i></a> ~ 2 Ma ago; an invasion by <a href="/wiki/Panamanian_night_monkey" title="Panamanian night monkey"><i>A. zonalis</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Geoffroy%27s_tamarin" title="Geoffroy's tamarin"><i>S. geoffroyi</i></a> ~ 1 Ma ago; a most recent invasion by <a href="/wiki/Black-headed_spider_monkey" title="Black-headed spider monkey"><i>A. fusciceps</i></a>. The species of the first wave have apparently been out-competed by those of the second, and now have much more restricted distributions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[135]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-172"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-172">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Salamander" title="Salamander">Salamanders</a> apparently dispersed to South America by the Early Miocene, about 23 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annum" title="Annum">Ma</a> ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elmer2013_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elmer2013-171">[138]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the salamander fauna of South America, which is restricted to the tropical region, consists of only 2 clades, and has fewer species and is far less diverse than that of much smaller Central America. Salamanders are believed to have originated in northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pangea" title="Pangea">Pangea</a>, perhaps not long before it separated to become <a href="/wiki/Laurasia" title="Laurasia">Laurasia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-early_amphibians_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-early_amphibians-162">[131]</a></sup> and are not present anywhere else in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> (see the <a href="/wiki/File:Cypron-Range_Caudata.svg" title="File:Cypron-Range Caudata.svg">world salamander distribution map</a>). In contrast, <a href="/wiki/Caecilian" title="Caecilian">caecilians</a> have a mostly <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwanan</a> <a href="/wiki/File:Distribution.gymnophiona.2.png" title="File:Distribution.gymnophiona.2.png">distribution</a>. Apart from a small region of overlap in southern China and northern Southeast Asia, Central America and northern South America are the only places in the world where both salamanders and caecilians are present.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-179"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-179">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is based on the definition of Sigmodontinae that excludes <a href="/wiki/Neotominae" title="Neotominae">Neotominae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tylomyinae" title="Tylomyinae">Tylomyinae</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-182"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-182">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i><a href="/wiki/Hippidion" title="Hippidion">Hippidion</a></i>, a relatively short-legged equid that developed in South America after invading from North America about 2.5 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annum" title="Annum">Ma</a> ago, has traditionally been thought to have evolved from <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_horse#Pliohippus" title="Evolution of the horse">pliohippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evolution_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evolution-180">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AncientDNA_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-AncientDNA-181">[146]</a></sup> However, recent studies of the <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> of <i>Hippidion</i> and other <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> Pleistocene horses indicate that <i>Hippidion</i> is actually a member of <i><a href="/wiki/Equus_(genus)" title="Equus (genus)">Equus</a></i>, closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Wild_horse" title="Wild horse">extant horse</a>, <i>E. ferus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evolution_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-Evolution-180">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AncientDNA_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-AncientDNA-181">[146]</a></sup> Another invasion of South America by <i>Equus</i> occurred about one Ma ago, and this lineage, traditionally viewed as the subgenus <i>Equus (Amerhippus)</i>, appears indistinguishable from <i>E. ferus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AncientDNA_181-2"><a href="#cite_note-AncientDNA-181">[146]</a></sup> Both these lineages became extinct at the end of the Pleistocene, but <i>E. ferus</i> was reintroduced from Eurasia by Europeans in the 16th century. Note: the authors of the DNA sequence study of <i>Equus (Amerhippus)</i> use "<i>E. caballus</i>" as an alternative specific name for "<i>E. ferus</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AncientDNA_181-3"><a href="#cite_note-AncientDNA-181">[146]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-184"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-184">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Not to be confused with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_mastodon" title="American mastodon">American mastodon</a> (<i>Mammut americanum</i>), a proboscid from a different family whose remains have been found no further south than <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[147]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-185"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-185">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sometimes classified as <a href="/wiki/Elephantidae" title="Elephantidae">elephantids</a> rather than as gomphotheres.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-190"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-190">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/South_American_gray_fox" title="South American gray fox">South American gray fox</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-202"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-202">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Condors apparently reached South America by the late Miocene or early Pliocene (4.5 – 6.0 Ma ago), several million years before the formation of the isthmus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Condor_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-Condor-201">[162]</a></sup> Condor-like forms in North America date back to the <a href="/wiki/Miocene#North_America" title="Miocene">Barstovian</a> <a href="/wiki/Stage_(stratigraphy)" title="Stage (stratigraphy)">stage</a> (middle Miocene, 11.8 – 15.5 Ma ago).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hadrogyps_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hadrogyps-200">[161]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
